  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_578ce201-e8e5-4710-9eeb-a637ed8fde68'

  <span id="freeText4533964590413692622" style="display:none">Still reeling from their experiences in Roanoke in 1600, Jonah and Katherine arrive in 1611 only moments before a mutiny on Henry Hudson’s ship in the icy waters of James Bay. But things are messed up: they’ve lost the real John Hudson, and they find what seems to be the fabled Northwest Passage—even though they are pretty sure that that route doesn’t actually exist. Will this new version of history replace the real past? Is this the end of time as we know it? With more at stake than ever before, Jonah and Katherine struggle to unravel the mysteries of 1611 and the Hudson Passage...before everything they know is lost.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_193420710" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/193420710" />
    <a title="Nerd-Light-Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5651221-nerd-light-books"><img alt="Nerd-Light-Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308348899p2/5651221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/193420710?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nerd-Light-Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nerd-Light-Books" href="/user/show/5651221-nerd-light-books">Nerd-Light-Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer193420710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10900438087399684894">After a tip from the author on her facebook page, I put my name in, and I got an advanced copy of this book! I was SO excited! I really love this series. <br/><br/>SPOILER ALERT! This book is part of a series. If you have not read Found, Sent and Sabotaged, read on at your own risk!<br/><br/>	Jonah and Katherine have been hurled through time yet again, and they have no idea where or when they are at first. They soon discover that they are on Henry Hudson’s ship, Discovery, and a mutiny is afoot. Jonah must disguise</span>
  <span id="freeText10900438087399684894" style="display:none">After a tip from the author on her facebook page, I put my name in, and I got an advanced copy of this book! I was SO excited! I really love this series. <br /><br />SPOILER ALERT! This book is part of a series. If you have not read Found, Sent and Sabotaged, read on at your own risk!<br /><br />	Jonah and Katherine have been hurled through time yet again, and they have no idea where or when they are at first. They soon discover that they are on Henry Hudson’s ship, Discovery, and a mutiny is afoot. Jonah must disguise himself as Hudson’s son, John, and Katherine hides by becoming invisible. Jonah and Katherine are thrust from one life-threatening situation to another in this fast paced tale. Jonah and Katherine don’t know who to trust, but they do know that history has been dramatically changed. In the past their missions have been to set history back on course, so that is what they set out to do once again, but they soon discover that someone is working against them. Time is very near collapsing, causing the end of all things past, present, and future. Will Jonah and Katherine be able to stop it?<br /><br />	I love the idea of this series: Missing children stolen from the point in time before they were lost, brought to the future and raised by foster parents as modern day kids. The first book, Found, is all about Jonah’s discovery of who he is. Just unraveling the mystery (which sets up the rest of the series) kept me completely enthralled. Several characters go back in time to England during the War of the Roses in the second book, Sent. I love this period of history, and again, I was very entertained and captivated by the story. In book three, Sabotaged, the characters travel back to the site of the Roanoke colony, but another element is introduced to the series as well. A villain from the future named Second, who is on a mission to make his own version of history, steps in to really complicate things. The reader isn’t really aware of Second or his plans until the end of book three, so things don’t get really confusing until book four, which is Torn. <br /><br />	To begin with, I didn’t really find Henry Hudson’s search for the infamous Northwest Passage a very intriguing historical subject. After all, we know he didn’t find one. But when I reached the end of the story, I found that Margaret Peterson Haddix had written lengthy author’s notes on what is known about Henry Hudson’s last voyage and the fate of the lost explorer. The real mystery is actually very interesting. But Haddix had so much to explain about Jonah and Katherine’s story; there wasn’t really time to delve into Hudson’s story. And even if there had been time it wouldn’t have mattered. Jonah and Katherine enter another version of history very early on in the book because Second makes changes and sets history on a new course. So Torn was lacking one of the things I love about the series, a way to learn about an actual historical event. The events in Torn were mostly created by Haddix. And the facts and tidbits that were true were things that I already knew. I will say, however, that I think most middle grade readers could learn something of history by reading this book. Younger readers have probably not read the amount of historical fiction I have or taken the advanced history classes that I have for that matter.<br /><br />	I still really enjoyed Haddix’s style. Her characters are very distinct and likable. I’ve come to know and love them, and they feel like real kids. I often complain that books about middle grade kids have characters that don’t act and think like middle grade kids. That is not the case in The Missing series. Although there are times when I question how much these kids remember about their social studies classes. (They must have awesome teachers at that school! Ha!) The pacing of the story is also excellent. It keeps moving at a fast clip. There’s never any time for the reader to get bored. There’s almost always some sort of action or danger afoot. And I love that Haddix doesn’t insult her readers by making the story too predictable. So far every book in this series has kept me guessing about what will happen right up until the very end. I have become a very analytical reader. It’s hard to surprise me, so that’s really saying something! This series should not be read out of order. So hopefully anyone reading Torn will have already read books one through three. The people reading this book are probably already fans, and if you are a fan of the Missing series, you will appreciate Torn for what it is: another fast paced adventure, another chance to get to spend some time with Jonah and Katherine, and a vehicle that keeps the series moving on! Yes, there are three more books in this series, and I am very glad for that. I just hope the next one happens in a more interesting time and place. I want to know what happens next, but I would also love to learn more about another one of history’s lesser known mysteries.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10900438087399684894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_301969878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/301969878" />
    <a title="Sabrina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina"><img alt="Sabrina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425694026p2/3536114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/301969878?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabrina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabrina " href="/user/show/3536114-sabrina">Sabrina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301969878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4263675696874560177"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373495i/727112.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>"There's another one" was the first thing that came to my mind when I stumbled upon this book at my library! It has been a long time since I have read a book by Haddix, primarily because her last installment in the series was ... disappointing. Nevertheless, I grabbed the copy and rushed home to finish the novel within a couple of hours. I had hoped that Ms. Haddix would blow me away as she did with her other novels such as Double Identity.<br/><br/>I was not blown away. More like a tiny little wind that </span>
  <span id="freeText4263675696874560177" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373495i/727112.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"There's another one" was the first thing that came to my mind when I stumbled upon this book at my library! It has been a long time since I have read a book by Haddix, primarily because her last installment in the series was ... disappointing. Nevertheless, I grabbed the copy and rushed home to finish the novel within a couple of hours. I had hoped that Ms. Haddix would blow me away as she did with her other novels such as Double Identity.<br><br>I was not blown away. More like a tiny little wind that had only enough power to make a pinwheel spin. <br><br>I am not saying it was a terrible book, it was good. It just wasn't as good as it could have been. <br><br>Maybe I had too high expectations or perhaps I was in a fowl mood but for whatever reason, I found Torn to be boring and dull. After the disappoinment from the last novel, I was in strong hopes that this fourth installment would capture my interest but it didn't.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373495i/727113.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, it seems that with the increase in novels, there is a decrease in interest. Then again, this novel is directed towards elementary and middle school children so perhaps my being in high school influenced my opinion on such book. But I do not think it should matter because I did enjoy the first of her series.<br><br>On the other side, my age did not help me understand some of the time travel smarty-pants things. I enjoyed that scientific part of the novel but I mainly nodded my head and pretended to understand when honestly, I had no clue what the paragraph meant. It's probably just me, I did feel stupid that day.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373495i/727114.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Enough of all that negativity! This book did earn 3 out of 5 stars! Why? Because despite my disappoint, the historical facts and the plot line were not bad. The character development of Jonah and Katherine was better, you can notice the book becoming more mature. And the suspense is all still there (even if the majority of the humor is robbed).<br><br>Jonah and Katherine are once again going through time and somehow end up on Henry Hudson's ship, Destiny and things are in chaos! Jonah is apparently John (Hudson's son) and Katherine, get this, can become invisible! I remember that special power, it still makes me smile at the ingenious of it! This time, she really is invisible though!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380373495i/727115.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As always, the pair go through various obstacles and challenges, all in an attempt to fix history and essentialy time. With the paradoxes and all that other science-things, time is threatened of being destroyed unless Jonah and Katherine can save it!<br> <br>I learned a lot because of this book, which is a mega plus! I do love history but I have never once heard of Henry Hudson (I'm Canadian so that might be a factor as to why I have not learned about him). Well, as in all of the Missing series, Haddix cleverly incorporates history into fiction to make the novel both educational and fun!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>Henry Hudson was searching for the Northwest passage during his last voyage when his crew went against him and ... who knows what happened to him? Haddix approaches this in a clever yet interesting way.<br> <br><br>The characters, as always, were fantastic! As always, Jonah is my favorite but Katherine is a close second! I am pleased that Jonah is 13 and he acts that way too, not overly mature or idiotic. <br><br>I am not going to reveal any spoilers but I will say that many unanswered questions regarding Jonah's and Katherine's story is resolved however, new ones are created. Haddix seems to enjoy suspense because she even made me want to know the answer!<br><br>What I truly enjoyed was all the twists and turns the plot took! As always, I didn't know what to expect and this unpredictable plot made the entire novel much more satasfying. I thought I knew was going to happen and then something completely different happens and this sudden surprise is <i>good</i>! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380912245i/3201362.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If only she spicened up some details, added some better dialogue and perhaps went a bit deeper in the historical aspect, this book would have been a winner!<br><br>I will now have to read the next novel due to the overwhelming amount of suspense and my stupid curiosity! You know what they say ... curiosity killed the cat! But satisfaction brought it back! Hopefully the next novel will have more interest, I find that if Haddix chooses a perhaps more interesting time in history (and place) the novel will be much more satasfying. <br><br>2 final thoughts:<br><br>1) Time travel is awesome<br>2) And so are cats<br><br><span>[image error]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4263675696874560177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1594781625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1594781625" />
    <a title="Julie Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1505281-julie-suzanne"><img alt="Julie Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491956923p2/1505281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1594781625?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Suzanne" href="/user/show/1505281-julie-suzanne">Julie Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1505281-julie-suzanne?shelf=ms-library">ms-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1505281-julie-suzanne?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1594781625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16686656146147207006">A Social Studies teacher and I read the first 3 books in this sci-fi/historical fiction blended series YEARS ago, and after the third book, we were content to discontinue the series. However, my student-lead book club chose the first book in the series, Found, for their monthly read. I was relieved that I had already read it and would not have to scramble to add it to my to-read pile. Win-win! However, 4 of my 6 students finished the book in record time, came into to library at lunch, passing pe</span>
  <span id="freeText16686656146147207006" style="display:none">A Social Studies teacher and I read the first 3 books in this sci-fi/historical fiction blended series YEARS ago, and after the third book, we were content to discontinue the series. However, my student-lead book club chose the first book in the series, Found, for their monthly read. I was relieved that I had already read it and would not have to scramble to add it to my to-read pile. Win-win! However, 4 of my 6 students finished the book in record time, came into to library at lunch, passing periods, after school etc. to speculate, rave, and wonder. They were HOOKED. They then started tearing through the series, and I made the mistake of telling them that I read it with the Social Studies teacher years ago, and even though they don't know him, they tracked him down to talk about the books. Before you know it, they're on book 4 (in less than a month) and the SS teacher and I are BACK IN. Unfortunately for me but wonderful for my students, there are now 8 books in this series. I think I'm stuck reading them all. <br />Anyway, this was a quick read compared to almost the entire series of Lunar Chronicles that I've been devouring for two weeks, and it was only an OKAY experience. I mean, it gives the reader a headache with all this time travel crap (I really hate dealing with time travel paradox--it's not for me), but I was compelled to finish it, although it may have been out of a sense of duty rather than the plot. <br />In short, the book was a solid 2 experience, but I'm going to have to finish the series and learn a bit about some history along with the headaches. Haddix's Missing Series is an absolute treasure to 7th graders who are into Dr. Who and are good readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16686656146147207006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1594781625">

    <a title="Eliot Morrison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59200119-eliot-morrison"><img alt="Eliot Morrison" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1781826488?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eliot Morrison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eliot Morrison" href="/user/show/59200119-eliot-morrison">Eliot Morrison</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1781826488" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16144897445320250331">I enjoyed this book very much. I highly recommend Torn because there are many twists and turns throughout the story that are unexpected. Each chapter the book pulls you deeper into the story and you don't want to stop reading. Jonah and his sister Katherine go back in time, following the story of explorer Henry Hudson and his son, John. The book details a very dangerous voyage to find the Northwest Passage, and many things happen that you would never expect. The book will have your heart pumping</span>
  <span id="freeText16144897445320250331" style="display:none">I enjoyed this book very much. I highly recommend Torn because there are many twists and turns throughout the story that are unexpected. Each chapter the book pulls you deeper into the story and you don't want to stop reading. Jonah and his sister Katherine go back in time, following the story of explorer Henry Hudson and his son, John. The book details a very dangerous voyage to find the Northwest Passage, and many things happen that you would never expect. The book will have your heart pumping. Like all books in the "The Missing" series, Torn has historical references that I find very interesting. However, because Torn is part of a series, if you haven't read the other books, some things mentioned can be quite confusing. My favorite character in the book by far was Jonah. Jonah cared not only about himself but others as well. Jonah always wanted to make sure his sister Katherine was safe. I admire the fact that Jonah would go out of his way to help others in their time of need.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16144897445320250331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18277158719138415741" style="display:none">In their other adventures, Jonah, Katherine and the missing kid have tracers, the ghostly outline of what's supposed to happen, to help steer them in the right direction.<br />Jonah and Katherine have no contact with J.B. or Second, no clue as to what to do, no idea if their actions are helping or hurting time.<br />Jonah and Katherine quickly find themselves in 1611, stuck on a sailing vessel off the icy coast of Canada, captained by the explorer Henry Hudson.<br />And when Second requires their help, Jonah and his sister, Katherine, don't have much choice but to comply, if they want to see J.B. and their friends again, who are stranded in the year 1600.<br />A mutiny breaks out on board, and the captain and a handful of sailors, including Jonah pretending to be John, are forced into a rowboat and left in the icy ocean to perish.<br />Unfortunately, the siblings don't have John Hudson with them this time; he just happens to have gone missing again.<br />Henry's son, John, is one of the missing kids of time.<br />Ever since he found out that he's part of a group of kidnapped babies snatched out of time, life has taken an adventurous turn.<br />Captain Henry Hudson is searching for a passage to the Orient, but the crew is near starvation and talking mutiny.<br />Jonah and Katherine struggle to figure out what choices to make.<br />So Jonah slips on a disguise and pretends to be the cabin boy, John.<br />Their Elucidator, a time traveler's communication and other apps tool, seems to be malfunctioning.<br />Thirteen-year-old Jonah longs for a normal life again.<br />But helping return the kids to when and where they belong, and restoring history along the way, is dangerous work.<br />Unfortunately, a wrong choice could set time unraveling, destroying everything and everyone.</span>

I really did. But the second half <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(let's make the second half start from the part Second appeared <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> crawled by on crutches. The first half was actually pretty good <s>except for the first few pages which were BORING </s>and were above my <s>low </s>expectations, but THEN we were plunged into this series's trademark headache-y, I-don't-care-about-that, you-caused-a-time-paradox-now-you-must-pay part where I tuned everything out and skimmed. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Yeah - Henry Hudson's got the biggest ego on the planet," Katherine said. "[...]Made me want to turn visible just so I could say, 'Guess what? Four hundred years from now, schoolkids are just going to get you mixed up with Vasco da Gama on tests. The really stupid ones aren't going to remember your name even when the question is, who discovered the Hudson River and the Hudson Bay?' "<br />Jonah thought maybe he'd done that once.</i>
</blockquote><br />I have to admit, I wanted to DNF this series after <i>Sabotaged</i>. <b>The time stuff was too paradox-y, and eventually you stopped caring about whatever was happening to the characters.</b> But in this book I actually cared about them; even some of the sailors (like Staffe). Maybe that's because in the first half the only main characters were Katherine and Jonah.<br /><blockquote>"𝓣𝓱𝓮 𝓶𝓪𝓼𝓽𝓮𝓻 𝓲𝓼 𝓵𝓲𝓴𝓮 𝓪 𝓼𝓽𝓻𝓪𝔀 𝓲𝓷 𝓽𝓱𝓮 𝔀𝓲𝓷𝓭, 𝓯𝓪𝓿𝓸𝓻𝓲𝓷𝓰 𝓯𝓲𝓻𝓼𝓽 𝓸𝓷𝓮 𝓶𝓪𝓷, 𝓽𝓱𝓮𝓷 𝓪𝓷𝓸𝓽𝓱𝓮𝓻, 𝓭𝓮𝓬𝓲𝓭𝓲𝓷𝓰 𝓷𝓸𝓽𝓱𝓲𝓷𝓰, 𝓪𝓷𝓰𝓮𝓻𝓲𝓷𝓰 𝓪𝓵𝓵."</blockquote><br />It was slow, I wanted to throw this book out of the window sometimes - <b>but hey! I actually liked it this time around.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11561614976118391674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1498526274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498526274" />
    <a title="MATT ABHOLD" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29797218-matt-abhold"><img alt="MATT ABHOLD" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498526274?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MATT ABHOLD" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MATT ABHOLD" href="/user/show/29797218-matt-abhold">MATT ABHOLD</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498526274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7893718202970036945">Personal Response: The book <i>Torn</i> is the fourth book by Haddix and it was pretty interesting. The author based this story off of Henry Hudson’s ship, and Jonah has to disguise himself as John Hudson; Henry Hudson’s son. This book is decent because the story line keeps changing, but the things that Jonah and Katherine have to do are very repetitive. 	<br/><br/>Plot: Jonah and Katherine are sent from 1600 to 1611 to <i>The Discovery</i>, Henry Hudson’s ship. They are put in the middle of a mutiny, but nobody notice</span>
  <span id="freeText7893718202970036945" style="display:none">Personal Response: The book <i>Torn</i> is the fourth book by Haddix and it was pretty interesting. The author based this story off of Henry Hudson’s ship, and Jonah has to disguise himself as John Hudson; Henry Hudson’s son. This book is decent because the story line keeps changing, but the things that Jonah and Katherine have to do are very repetitive. 	<br /><br />Plot: Jonah and Katherine are sent from 1600 to 1611 to <i>The Discovery</i>, Henry Hudson’s ship. They are put in the middle of a mutiny, but nobody notices them. The crew is taking over the ship and they are casting Hudson and his closest men away. Jonah and Katherine leave with them to restore time to its original state. There are forces working against them though, and they don’t get it right. The crew takes over the ship again, and Hudson is determined to find the Northwest Passage. It doesn’t really exist but the ship sails on and they actually find it. Time is working against everybody, and Jonah and Katherine get a chance to steer Hudson away and they take it. They go back in time to the mutiny, and play through again. This time, they get it right, and they can now go back to save their friends from 1605. Once they get the Elucidator to JB, he sends them back to their normal time in the 21st century where they are safe. <br /><br />Characterization: Jonah is the main character and is Katherine's big brother. He fell in love with Andrea at the beginning of the book and end of the previous book, but he gets friendzoned. He is getting smarter and starting to think more reasonably when he is in difficult situations, which comes with him getting older. <br /><br />Katherine is growing up also, and you can tell because she stays a lot more calm when Jonah needs her to be. There aren’t a lot of responsibilities for Katherine in this book, so she doesn’t have to overcome anything. She stays by Jonah’s side throughout the whole book though and Jonah is glad.<br /><br />Second is the last main character in this book. He unravels time and that is why Jonah and Katherine have to go to 1611. He is the one working against Jonah and Katherine while on the ship. He has an immense knowledge of time travel and is way ahead of Jonah and Katherine.<br /><br />Setting: This story is set in 1611 on board <i>The Discovery</i> in the Hudson Bay. This plays a big difference because Jonah and Katherine get really cold and hungry and there isn’t anything they can do about it. <br /><br />Theme: The theme of this story is trust. In the beginning, Second earns Jonah and Katherine’s trust by offering them a deal. If they can split time, they can save their friends and they will never see him again. He follows through with the deal, but he is working against them while they are trying to help him, so they should be more careful with who they trust.<br /><br />Age: I recommend this book to those over the age of 13 and who are into science fiction because it has a confusing story line that jumps around a lot, but it has really good historical references. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7893718202970036945" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_219772343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219772343" />
    <a title="Dreamergirl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4961397-dreamergirl"><img alt="Dreamergirl" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/219772343?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dreamergirl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dreamergirl" href="/user/show/4961397-dreamergirl">Dreamergirl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961397-dreamergirl?shelf=thriller-adventure-mystery">thriller-adventure-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961397-dreamergirl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961397-dreamergirl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961397-dreamergirl?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4961397-dreamergirl?shelf=sci-fiction">sci-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219772343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7127572114249998476">Sure, after reading "Sent" I thought this series was going to be good, after all no one in the genre writes better than Margaret Haddix, but this book was so nothing like the writing I remembered from "Sent". Not in a bad way...it was far better! The characters that I thought I knew were introduced to me again in a totally different outlook and I had to remind myself a few times that it was only a book that I was reading. The history was also much more exciting and captivating than in "Sent" and</span>
  <span id="freeText7127572114249998476" style="display:none">Sure, after reading "Sent" I thought this series was going to be good, after all no one in the genre writes better than Margaret Haddix, but this book was so nothing like the writing I remembered from "Sent". Not in a bad way...it was far better! The characters that I thought I knew were introduced to me again in a totally different outlook and I had to remind myself a few times that it was only a book that I was reading. The history was also much more exciting and captivating than in "Sent" and I felt impressed at the amazing way Haddix had me guessing till the very end. The only thing that kind of made the plot obvious was when she said that "Pattrick" killed one of the sailors, I knew right away that "Patrick" was actually Second back in the game. One tiny thing that I was left a bit confused with was how Andrea and the main character's friends (who were in a different period) had aged so much while they were in time and why they didn't get back to their own time right away, but I guess that's just a part of time-travel. I must have also skipped something in my excitement for what would happen next and how the author would end "Torn". It was not like the confusing parts and the holes in the plot of "Sent" though. Surprisingly I found the ending quite satisfying. Here is my review:<br /><br />Jonah and Katherine knew they were going back in time, but they didn't realize that their only way of communication with J.B. back in the twenty-first century would stop working or know that they'd find themselves in the middle of a ship... and an ugly mutiny. The sailors are worn out, sick, and a lot of them look as if they are near death. They have little food left and the captian, Henry Hudson, seems to think that they must go on and find the NorthWest Passage no matter what so that he will wash up in the glory. Jonah is disguised as John Hudson, the son of the captian and soon secrets are revealed to him that change their mission completely and Jonah starts to doubt if he will ever see any of his friends... and most importantly Andrea again. The faith of the world... and possibly all of time is in the hands of two thirteen-year olds and let me tell you they are the best hands that have ever touched it... <br /><br />Have you ever known those books, that just by re-reading them, they leave you not able to imagine how you ever read anything else, as if they scrubbed some of their quality onto you and make you feel kind of like you were in the story? That's how I felt after I finished "Torn". Not many books can make you feel that, and certainly "Sent" didn't, but I must have not choosen the right book to read by Margaret before. This one will blow you away. I will surely be back for more... <br /><br />I'd recommend...</span>
  <a data-text-id="7127572114249998476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1109156143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109156143" />
    <a title="Robert Karbowiak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34820697-robert-karbowiak"><img alt="Robert Karbowiak" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109156143?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robert Karbowiak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robert Karbowiak" href="/user/show/34820697-robert-karbowiak">Robert Karbowiak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109156143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11793907291176275810">Torn, the predecessor of the book Caught, by Margaret Peterson Haddix is one of the authors best works. I have read the entire series, and have loved this book the most. Haddix, by my opinion, is one of the greatest authors alive today. Her works today are very probably regarded as beautiful works of modern art. Haddix takes a different approach than many of the authors we know today. The literary element "deux ex machine" is regarded as one of the worst, because it is shown as a plot twist, in </span>
  <span id="freeText11793907291176275810" style="display:none">Torn, the predecessor of the book Caught, by Margaret Peterson Haddix is one of the authors best works. I have read the entire series, and have loved this book the most. Haddix, by my opinion, is one of the greatest authors alive today. Her works today are very probably regarded as beautiful works of modern art. Haddix takes a different approach than many of the authors we know today. The literary element "deux ex machine" is regarded as one of the worst, because it is shown as a plot twist, in which the author is most probably stumped for an ending or a scene. Haddix is not afraid to incorporate this into the story, because even though regarded as a show of weakness, this element adds to the almost magnetic-like attractive personality of the story, and the characters themselves. Jonah and Katherine are locked in a struggle to uncover Jonah's identity after finding out that Jonah is a person who was otherwise well known on earth. He was kidnapped from the past by time travelers seeking evil purposes and brought to the future. People would pay big bucks to someone who had the genes related to some of the most influential people of history. Jonah and Katherine, so far, have returned their best friend Chip and his brother from the past, who was separated from him during the time travel, to their original time period. They had returned Andrea, a pretty girl Jonah had a crush on since first sight, to her proper time in the 1600s. Jonah was growing more and more impatient to find out his own identity so he can finally put this all behind him and forget this ever happened so he could move on with his life, which was often filled with the monotony of any other teenager's life. Will Jonah find his identity in this book? You'll just have to read and find out for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11793907291176275810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436240474" />
    <a title="Neil R. Coulter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22306206-neil-r-coulter"><img alt="Neil R. Coulter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592517121p2/22306206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436240474?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil R. Coulter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil R. Coulter" href="/user/show/22306206-neil-r-coulter">Neil R. Coulter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22306206-neil-r-coulter?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436240474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14717987490688432716">Another good entry in Margaret Peterson Haddix's <em>Missing</em> series. Haddix is a great storyteller, and one of the things I like most about this series is her skill in introducing new twists in a natural, organic way. Each book in this series has upped the stakes just a little bit, by introducing new characters, conspiracies, or challenges for Jonah and Katherine. In a lot of stories, this constant upping of the game feels artificial, but Haddix is good at constructing series in which each new chall</span>
  <span id="freeText14717987490688432716" style="display:none">Another good entry in Margaret Peterson Haddix's <em>Missing</em> series. Haddix is a great storyteller, and one of the things I like most about this series is her skill in introducing new twists in a natural, organic way. Each book in this series has upped the stakes just a little bit, by introducing new characters, conspiracies, or challenges for Jonah and Katherine. In a lot of stories, this constant upping of the game feels artificial, but Haddix is good at constructing series in which each new challenge makes sense within the world she has created. This is only the halfway point in the <em>Missing</em> series, and I'm very much looking forward to seeing what further twists and turns she has in store as the series continues.<br /><br />The focus of <em>Torn</em> is explorer Henry Hudson and his son, John. I didn't know much about their final voyage, so the historical information was all new, and interesting, to me. Jonah has a new challenge in this story, and time itself is unraveling, so no one is quite sure how the events are supposed to proceed. Though there are some father/son issues in the book, I felt that the emotional effect of that relationship was not quite as poignant as in the previous book's relationship between Virginia Dare and her grandfather. Also, I really couldn't believe that it took Jonah and Katherine so long to figure out that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Prickett was actually Second <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I mean, really. That should have been obvious to them <em>much</em> earlier.<br /><br />Even with those flaws, however, I enjoyed <em>Torn</em> very much, and went right into the next book, <em>Caught</em>, as soon as I finished <em>Torn</em>. This is a really fine series, and I recommend it for upper-elementary ages and older.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14717987490688432716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Jonas and Katherine teens from present day travel back in time to help Henry Hudson find the middle passage.   <span id="freeText4279685035544904972" style="display:none">Torn<br />by Margaret Peterson Haddix<br /><br />Torn, by Margaret Peterson Haddix is a historical fiction novel that is full of action, and adventure. Jonas and Katherine teens from present day travel back in time to help Henry Hudson find the middle passage. Jonah and Katherine find conflict aboard Henry Hudson ship, while they are trying to fix time there is a mutiny aboard and something strange is happening below deck... Will Jonah and Katherine be able to save time, and themselves?<br /><br />I thought this was a great story that is thrilling, full of danger,and teaches you about history. The text states "Something very strange and dangerous is happening on the Discovery"(94). This adds a little mystery and suspense to the great action, adventure, and history in the novel.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who enjoys learning about history, and likes a good suspenseful mystery. This book is appropriate for grades 6 and up because there is some violence in the novel. This is a great read and a fantastic story by Margaret Peterson Haddix.</span>

<div id="review_2403844707" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2403844707" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26821526-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595092257p2/26821526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2403844707?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/26821526-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11348546-torn">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2403844707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17880027856098443267">As a fourth grade teacher, I find this novel to be indescribably important. As soon as I finished reading it, I immediately started writing a Donors Choose project to try to get a class set (link here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.donorschoose.org/project/time-travels-for-fourth-graders/3350828/?challengeid=334861&givingCartId=7639702&utm_source=dc&utm_medium=page&utm_campaign=project&utm_term=teacher_2107100&rf=page-dc-2018-06-project-teacher_2107100'>https://www.donorschoose.org/project/...</a>)<br/><br/>Ms. Haddix has a remarkable way of drawing readers in to this incredible tale of exploration through two beautifully crafted characters in the form of adolescent time travelers. Her art of writing made me believe, even as an adult, that I was right there wi</span>
  <span id="freeText17880027856098443267" style="display:none">As a fourth grade teacher, I find this novel to be indescribably important. As soon as I finished reading it, I immediately started writing a Donors Choose project to try to get a class set (link here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.donorschoose.org/project/time-travels-for-fourth-graders/3350828/?challengeid=334861&amp;givingCartId=7639702&amp;utm_source=dc&amp;utm_medium=page&amp;utm_campaign=project&amp;utm_term=teacher_2107100&amp;rf=page-dc-2018-06-project-teacher_2107100">https://www.donorschoose.org/project/...</a>)<br /><br />Ms. Haddix has a remarkable way of drawing readers in to this incredible tale of exploration through two beautifully crafted characters in the form of adolescent time travelers. Her art of writing made me believe, even as an adult, that I was right there with the protagonists trying to fix history and figure out how to handle a serious division in crew on Hudson’s expedition that could alter lives and history as a whole. <br /><br />I’ve taught European exploration to fourth graders for three years now, and for some reason, the concept of mutiny is unfathomable to them. I finally feel like I have the tool to help them grasp the predicament that caused Henry Hudson’s trip to end in the manner in which it did. <br /><br />Thank you, Ms. Haddix! You have given me a precious gift with this tale, and I can’t wait to have my own copies to pass on that special gift to my sweet kiddos!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17880027856098443267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2521258537" />
    <a title="Curran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/86407739-curran"><img alt="Curran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536257050p2/86407739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2521258537?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Curran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Curran" href="/user/show/86407739-curran">Curran</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2521258537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5128803948819615221">Jonah and Katherine go on yet another trip through time, back to the 1600’s, to Roanoke City, with Dare the Dog and Andrea/Virginia Dare. <br/><br/>Torn is book #4 in “The Missing” series. It is a science fiction book, that will keep you on the edge of your seat, due to the unexpected twists and turns throughout the story. <br/><br/>Jonah is an adopted boy from the past, who doesn’t know his true identity. Katherine is Jonah’s younger sister. Their mission is to return children who were taken from time periods and </span>
  <span id="freeText5128803948819615221" style="display:none">Jonah and Katherine go on yet another trip through time, back to the 1600’s, to Roanoke City, with Dare the Dog and Andrea/Virginia Dare. <br /><br />Torn is book #4 in “The Missing” series. It is a science fiction book, that will keep you on the edge of your seat, due to the unexpected twists and turns throughout the story. <br /><br />Jonah is an adopted boy from the past, who doesn’t know his true identity. Katherine is Jonah’s younger sister. Their mission is to return children who were taken from time periods and returned back to their original identity. They both are caring and observant of the faint tracer lights that tell them what happened in the original time.<br /><br />Time is a theme throughout the book - they physically travel through time, they have to keep time stable or else all of time will collapse and understand how precious time really is.<br /><br />It was so good, that I could not put it down, but there were parts where I got frustrated, such as when Second was using time as a puppet. I was also excited when Jonah and Katherine figured out that Pricket was Second! I think Torn could be challenging to readers who don’t have the background knowledge of time and space. I would suggest it for readers in 5th grade and higher.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5128803948819615221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2782289205" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2782289205" />
    <a title="Evey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/88813044-evey"><img alt="Evey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2782289205?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evey" href="/user/show/88813044-evey">Evey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2782289205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4441063268142898382">The book was a spectacular combination of a complicated web of time travel which Haddix spins so wonderfully and a confused world of a teenage boy. I have a theory that JB, knowing what Jonah likes and (in my imagination) looks like an older version of Jonah, so that lead on to the thought, is JB Jonah but from the future? In the end of the book, JB claims to have known where Jonah was going from what Jonah was doing and said to him “ have fun... while you still can.” Of course this could all be</span>
  <span id="freeText4441063268142898382" style="display:none">The book was a spectacular combination of a complicated web of time travel which Haddix spins so wonderfully and a confused world of a teenage boy. I have a theory that JB, knowing what Jonah likes and (in my imagination) looks like an older version of Jonah, so that lead on to the thought, is JB Jonah but from the future? In the end of the book, JB claims to have known where Jonah was going from what Jonah was doing and said to him “ have fun... while you still can.” Of course this could all be from being from the future and being able to view the past, but I think not. Also, since JB is not that older than Jonah, that could mean that if I am proven correct in the next few books, then time travel could be invented while Jonah is in his late teens or early twenties. I just haven’t had anyone to share my theory with and hope you guys keep reading the books.</span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3363411440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12438893545095874649">I don't know how I feel about this book, I mean, I really like Margaret Peterson Haddix and I like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227651.Among_the_Hidden__Shadow_Children___1_' title='Among the Hidden (Shadow Children, #1) by Margaret Peterson Haddix' rel='nofollow noopener'>Among the Hidden</a>, it's just this book doesn't stand out. I feel like everything is the book is very shallow, and doesn't have depth to it. This also might be the first time I've read books in a series back-to-back, but I don't have the fifth book or the first book. Also, I feel like this book was disconnected and it kept breaking off into so many paths. It got to the point where I still don't know </span>
  <span id="freeText12438893545095874649" style="display:none">I don't know how I feel about this book, I mean, I really like Margaret Peterson Haddix and I like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227651.Among_the_Hidden__Shadow_Children___1_" title="Among the Hidden (Shadow Children, #1) by Margaret Peterson Haddix" rel="nofollow noopener">Among the Hidden</a>, it's just this book doesn't stand out. I feel like everything is the book is very shallow, and doesn't have depth to it. This also might be the first time I've read books in a series back-to-back, but I don't have the fifth book or the first book. Also, I feel like this book was disconnected and it kept breaking off into so many paths. It got to the point where I still don't know what happens at the end. Overall, this was an okay read. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KFQUJp57QnwN8YpKPQM01XqW5kIPo5leCdo9UQRYVz5uURHlJJ4Xf1bNnJ3E/R1jdwrp4/jFU4PHFdTkI+2JcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('w6MYhWkdHAoc8osIeiWuQ4l0He13C2igkPFqr/Nh/ACFph1G0/hJCUfOnd+D24f1hOgSTIBton1ePoMa1NQiTg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix">About Margaret Peterson Haddix</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1309842407p3/14617.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/14617.Margaret_Peterson_Haddix">Margaret Peterson Haddix
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3258606033075911032">Margaret Peterson Haddix grew up on a farm near Washington Court House, Ohio. She graduated from Miami University (of Ohio) with degrees in English/journalism, English/creative writing and history. Before her first book was published, she worked as a newspaper copy editor in Fort Wayne, Indiana; a newspaper reporter in Indianapolis; and a community college instructor and freelance writer in Danvil</span>
  <span id="freeText3258606033075911032" style="display:none">Margaret Peterson Haddix grew up on a farm near Washington Court House, Ohio. She graduated from Miami University (of Ohio) with degrees in English/journalism, English/creative writing and history. Before her first book was published, she worked as a newspaper copy editor in Fort Wayne, Indiana; a newspaper reporter in Indianapolis; and a community college instructor and freelance writer in Danville, Illinois. <br /><br /> She has since written more than 25 books for kids and teens, including <i>Running Out of Time</i>; <i>Don’t You Dare Read This, Mrs. Dunphrey</i>; <i>Leaving Fishers</i>; <i>Just Ella</i>; <i>Turnabout</i>; <i>Takeoffs and Landings</i>; <i>The Girl with 500 Middle Names</i>; <i>Because of Anya</i>; <i>Escape from Memory</i>; <i>Say What?</i>; <i>The House on the Gulf</i>; <i>Double Identity</i>; <i>Dexter the Tough</i>; <i>Uprising</i>; <i>Palace of Mirrors</i>; <i>Claim to Fame</i>; the <i>Shadow Children</i> series; and the <i>Missing</i> series. She also wrote <i>Into the Gauntlet</i>, the tenth book in the <i>39 Clues</i> series. Her books have been honored with <i>New York Times</i> bestseller status, the International Reading Association’s Children’s Book Award; American Library Association Best Book and Quick Pick for Reluctant Young Adult Readers notations; and more than a dozen state reader’s choice awards.<br /><br /><br /> Haddix and her husband, Doug, now live in Columbus, Ohio, with their two children.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3258606033075911032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
